--
-- Table structure for table `blog_tab`
--

CREATE TABLE `blog_tab` (
  `sn` int NOT NULL,
  `blog_id` varchar(20) NOT NULL,
  `cat_id` varchar(20) NOT NULL,
  `blog_title` mediumtext NOT NULL,
  `blog_url` varchar(255) NOT NULL,
  `seo_keywords` text NOT NULL,
  `seo_describtion` text NOT NULL,
  `blog_detail` longtext NOT NULL,
  `status_id` varchar(50) NOT NULL,
  `blog_pix` varchar(255) NOT NULL,
  `user_id` varchar(30) NOT NULL,
  `views` int NOT NULL,
  `reg_date` datetime NOT NULL,
  `last_updated` timestamp NOT NULL DEFAULT CURRENT_TIMESTAMP ON UPDATE CURRENT_TIMESTAMP
);

With 371 ethnic groups; each having peculiarities in ways of dressing, religious worship, dialects and socio-cultural dynamics, it&rsquo;s not surprising that there is a large diversity even in the traditional culinary preferences of these ethnic groups.</span></p>\r\n<p dir=\"ltr\" style=\"line-height: 1.3800000000000001; text-align: justify; margin-top: 0pt; margin-bottom: 10pt;\"><span style=\"font-size: 12pt; font-family: Calibri,sans-serif; color: #000000; background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\">Like many other places in the world, Nigerian foods and cooking styles derive significantly from the natural food items and spices that are cultivable in the natural climate and soil of each part of the country. This invariably contributes to the wide range of foods and how diverse they are from one part of the country to another. After all, people eat more of what grows and is available in their locality.&nbsp;</span></p>\r\n<p dir=\"ltr\" style=\"line-height: 1.3800000000000001; text-align: justify; margin-top: 0pt; margin-bottom: 10pt;\"><span style=\"font-size: 12pt; font-family: Calibri,sans-serif; color: #000000; background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\">Hence, while many food ingredients are common in many places across Nigeria, there are other ones that are only available in specific areas. Even with the common ones, the derivatives from them and the way they are prepared vary from one ethnic group to another. For instance, while Cassava is a common tuber in the Western and Eastern parts of the country, what are made from it in the west could be different from the foods made from it in the eastern part. Yorubas from the western part of the country make their cassava grits (garri) in the natural form, producing relatively white crunchy grits, while Ibos from the eastern part add some palm oil in the processing to produce yellow dry grits. Interestingly -over the years &ndash; social mingling and cross-cultural marriages have increasingly resulted in cross-acceptance of each of the variants by the other ethnic group.&nbsp;</span></p>\r\n<p dir=\"ltr\" style=\"line-height: 1.3800000000000001; text-align: justify; margin-top: 0pt; margin-bottom: 10pt;\"><span style=\"font-size: 12pt; font-family: Calibri,sans-serif; color: #000000; background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\">This cross-acceptance is not just peculiar to garri, but many other ethnic cuisines which were unique to an ethnic group are now being embraced by other ethnic groups in the country.</span></p>\r\n<p dir=\"ltr\" style=\"line-height: 1.3800000000000001; margin-top: 0pt; margin-bottom: 10pt;\"><span style=\"font-size: 12pt; font-family: Calibri,sans-serif; color: #000000; background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\">Generally, Nigerian foods are prepared from crops, grains, tubers and vegetables with palm oil or groundnut oil and spices used to flavor the soups and sauces.&nbsp;</span></p>\r\n<p dir=\"ltr\" style=\"line-height: 1.3800000000000001; margin-top: 0pt; margin-bottom: 10pt;\"><span style=\"font-size: 12pt; font-family: Calibri,sans-serif; color: #000000; background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\">Truly, long before independence, Nigeria&rsquo;s local communities had thrived on these foods at their localities.   `sn` int NOT NULL,

  `product_name` varchar(150) NOT NULL,
  `product_desc` text NOT NULL,
  `status_id` varchar(20) NOT NULL,
  `date` datetime NOT NULL
);

-- --------------------------------------------------------

--
-- Table structure for table `stock_tab`
--

CREATE TABLE `stock_tab` (
  `sn` int NOT NULL,
  `product_id` varchar(50) NOT NULL,
  `purchase_price` double NOT NULL,
  `selling_price` double NOT NULL,
  `profit` double NOT NULL,
  `available_qty` int NOT NULL,
  `outstanding_qty` int NOT NULL,
  `date` datetime NOT NULL
);

-- Dumping data for table `stock_tab`
